<Rate>5<//Rate>< Review>
Looking for a decent place to eat in the little town of Gonzales on the way up Highway 101. This one caught my eye from the reviews which all seemed favorable.  We were greatly surprised to find out that it was even more than favorable. The food was excellent, the service was friendly and prompt, the prices were cheap! What more could anyone ask? Some favorites were the shrimp cocktail. That one is more like a gazpacho soup that is loaded with shrimp! Another was the super Chavela. Also well loaded with everything and then some.</Review>

<rating>5</rating>< text>
This place has great service and great food. Whether you want breakfast, lunch, or dinner, the food will be delicious.

In the weekends, I like eating their Menudo. It is not greasy. The tripe is cut into small squares.

They serve foods for all types of weather. If it's hot, you can eat a shrimp cocktail. If it's cold, you can eat "Caldo de Pollo", "Siege Mares". This is a great place to be at. The waitresses are very helpful and polite.<//text>

<GmapID>0x80dcd75286da388b:0x5cfe75d87e893001</GmapID><review>I want to start out this review by telling you a little about me, so that the context makes more sense. I grew up in Southern California - Dana Point - and during my youth we had things like auto shop, wood shop, metal shop and other shop activities in school that encouraged sweat equity as a learning experience. Although were I grew up was rather affluent, having Scottish in my genes meant that we saved money. So I learned quite a bit about how mechanics worked, how things functioned around the house, and how to un-screwup something I'd previously ... screwed.

So changing a lock isn't a big deal. Neither is rekeying one.

Rekeying six well-worn 10-year old commercial locks so that they work with a new key while continuing to work with a master key seemed a bit above my pay grade. I could certainly take them out ... but the whole rekeying thing made me feel a bit uncomfortable.

I've taken locks to locksmith shops before. I've met the edgy fellows with metal burr etched dirty hands that smell of old tri-flow oil and teflon ... and even older sweat. You know; the guys who give you a price based on the clothes you're wearing measured against the desperation you exude because you don't know anything about the dark arts and magic of locksmithery. So I was prepared for what to expect when I went to head over to this shop that opened unusually early for a trade (8:30am).

This store is COMPLETELY the opposite of any other locksmith that I've ever been to. The store was neat, tidy, well laid out with products, swept floors, and an unexpectedly professional attitude and veneer.

Jim Thorpe was the gentleman who helped me out. I have NEVER met someone who knows as much about locks and who is willing to share his knowledge so that I felt comfortable and reassured that the job would be done right.

I gave him the six locks (in individual baggies numbers so I remembered where I got them from). He checked them all out in front of me, jumped on his computer after I gave him the address where the locks were from and said they'd been to that address before, and even cut a new master key from their records to make sure that it worked as well as the older master I included with the old locks. The new one worked WAY better.

He gave be a quote - in writing - as well as a time that the locks would be done by THAT DAY! I gave him the locks and went off to attend to the rest of my adventures for that morning.

A short while later - and well before the promised time - Jim gave me a call, and said that the locks were done and I could head over to pick them all up. I was shocked!

When I got back to the busy store, Jim had my order ready, remembered me, and then launched into an explanation of what he'd done. He explained about the locks (they were worn, and could do with a full servicing at some point), the new keys, and the new master he cut. He even managed to get the locks back in the original baggies instead of mixing them all up. THAT is attention to detail!

I got back to the building, installed the new locks, and they work perfectly! The new master works on the various locks in the building, and I am absolutely THRILLED with the whole process.

I HIGHLY recommend A-Abbot Locksmith for all your key needs. These guys are professional, quick, and they get the job done right the first time. If you get a chance, talk with Jim; he is not only knowledgeable, but he is willing to share that knowledge so that you know exactly what you're getting!</review>< Time>
